<snip>

> Over the years (starting from before STRING was available) I tried many ways 
> to insert long strings into COBOL programs. I'm sure most COBOL programmers 
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Whatever one may (or may not) think about the '02 ISO COBOL Standard, I *REALLY* 
like the fix for continuing alphanumeric literals, i.e.

   "ABC"-
   "defg  "-
   "x"

Allows you to NOT count where the "R-margin" or the continuation column or 
trailing blanks are.

It is worth nothing this is QUITE different from the (X/Open and some compilers 
as an extension)

   "ABC" &
   "defg  " &
   "x"

which is treated as one alphanumeric literal at "run-time" but as 3 separate 
text words for COPY/REPLACING and REPLACE.
```

> text words for COPY/REPLACING and REPLACE.

The above seems to suggest that concatenation
is not available in ISO/IEC 1989:2002 COBOL.
See page 118, 8.7.3 Concatenation operator,
"The concatenation operator is the COBOL
character '&', which shall be immediately
preceded and followed by a separator space."
```

```
Sorry if I was unclear. I meant to say that many implementors provided "&" 
concatenation as an extension to the '85 Standard - as this was what X/Open 
specified (and it was an '85 Standard based specification).  It is absolutely 
true that it is part of the '02 Standard (and that is where the new format 
continuation came in BECAUSE concatenation uses separate text words)
```

>
>
…[42 more quoted lines elided]…
>for multiple tests.

Another nice thing about this is that you can use the POINTER clause to set
the length, eg...

move 1 to input-ptr
string 'stuff goes here. '
       'more stuff here. '
       'even more stuff.'
  delimited by size
  into input-data
  with pointer input-ptr
subtract 1 from input-ptr giving input-data-length

Pretty cool.

Frank

_(thread depth: 16)_

- **From:** LX-i <lxi0007@netscape.net>

- **Message-ID:** `<993f0$459ae651$454920f8$20533@KNOLOGY.NET>`
- **In-Reply-To:** `<4vvj6uF1dqm00U2@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4v33ipF1a006cU1@mid.individual.net> <12oosqtmgaqcd81@news.supernews.com> <4v7ajgF1bf6u8U1@mid.individual.net> <1166980834.471149.102990@i12g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <4v8qu1F1b75r0U1@mid.individual.net> <dElkh.4094$yx6.3439@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net> <4vf0t1F1bfj5nU1@mid.individual.net> <4vfl66F1as7a4U1@mid.individual.net> <4vgj6mF1a4g7nU1@mid.individual.net> <4vimr5F1cedo7U1@mid.individual.net> <4vj2kkF1co1akU1@mid.individual.net> <4vlbkiF1bf56sU1@mid.individual.net> <4vlnqgF1c247oU1@mid.individual.net> <4vm6ldF16ggd7U1@mid.individual.net> <12pdftt926l3sb9@corp.supernews.com> <4vvj6uF1dqm00U2@mid.individual.net>`

```
Frank Swarbrick wrote:
> Another nice thing about this is that you can use the POINTER clause to set
> the length, eg...
…[10 more quoted lines elided]…
> Pretty cool.

Very cool.  We use it when we're building XML extract files for 
interfaces (which, since it's the mandated "thou shalt" format, we're 
doing more and more).  It keeps us from having to use fixed-length 
records (although some of the lazier guys have still been doing that... 
grrr.....).

Anyway, I usually do something like this - say the data we're supposed 
to send is tagged with "SerialNumber".

-8<-

move 1 to wsPtr
string "<SerialNumber" delimited by size
   into wsBuildArea
     with pointer wsPtr
end-string

if wsSerialNumber = spaces
     string " />" delimited by size
       into wsBuildArea
         with pointer wsPtr
     end-string
else
     string ">"  wsSerialNumber  "</SerialNumber>" delimited by space
       into wsBuildArea
         with pointer wsPtr
     end-string
end-if

->8-

At this point, wsPtr now has the length of the build area, which can be 
used to write a variable-length record, or used to string piece-meal 
into an output accrual area.

And to think, when STRING was developed, XML didn't even exist!  :) 
There are several things in COBOL that are like this too - they didn't 
exist, but the facilities that exist are great for it.
```

```
 Pete Dashwood<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> 12/29/06 9:01 PM >>>
>
>"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message 
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
>The hard parts were confining myself to the B margin and using upper
case...
>
>Fortunately the sun has come out and I'm off to a cocktail party so it
might 
>not be perfect. I ran it and checked the output; (the ARGUMENTS array)...
it 
>looked good.
>
>You may need to remove all the *> comments if your compiler doesn't support

>them; the rest should compile OK.
>
>Should be able to cut and paste the code below directly into your editor.
It 
>should run as written.

Code deleted

I had to make one minor change to make this work:

INSPECT NV-WORK
   TALLYING MYTALLY1 FOR CHARACTERS
        BEFORE MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR 

has to be changed to

INSPECT NV-WORK (1:STRING-PARM-LEN)
   TALLYING MYTALLY1 FOR CHARACTERS
        BEFORE MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR 

Or you could probably keep the original inspect and change the IF statement
from
IF MYTALLY1 = STRING-PARM-LEN

to

IF MYTALLY1 = FUNCTION LENGTH(NV-WORK)

Though I didn't try that one out.  I prefer the former.

In any case, and don't take this the wrong way, your result isn't actually
what I was looking for.  What I wanted, and pretty much knew was not
possible, was to get the two fields INPUT-STRING-ID and INPUT-STRING-PARM
set based solely on a single UNSTRING.  No temporary fields (NV-WORK)
allowed.  Of course I did not state that explicitly, so you couldn't have
been expected to know.

I actually originally had something similar to what you had.  I used a
second UNSTRING instead of the INSPECT followed by MOVE.  Reworking your
example, it might have looked something like this...

     PERFORM                                        
        VARYING ARGS-X1                             
           FROM 1                                   
             BY 1                                   
        UNTIL ARGS-X1 > MAX-ARGUMENTS OR            
              INPUT-DATA-POS > INPUT-DATA-LENGTH    
           MOVE SPACES TO NV-WORK                   
           UNSTRING                                 
              INPUT-DATA                            
                 DELIMITED BY MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER   
                    INTO NV-WORK                    
                 COUNT IN STRING-PARM-LEN           
                 WITH POINTER INPUT-DATA-POS        
           END-UNSTRING                             
           IF STRING-PARM-LEN = ZERO                
              SET ARG-END-OF-GROUP (ARGS-X1) TO TRUE
           ELSE                                     
              UNSTRING                              
                 NV-WORK (1:STRING-PARM-LEN)        
                    DELIMITED BY MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR
                       INTO ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1)      
                            ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1)     
              END-UNSTRING                          
           END-IF
     END-PERFORM 

(Everything before and after this loop is unchanged.)

The thing I like about my original method, other than requiring two
unstrings, is that no temporary field is required.

Anyway, thanks for giving it a shot!

Frank


--- 
Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA
```

> been expected to know.

:-) I guessed as much but I took you at your word... :-)

This whole (thoroughly enjoyable) exercise made me think about a few 
things...

I mentioned somewhere else recently that when we are dealing with code based 
solutions we tend to think in terms of a code based solution.

In this case you were thinking about using UNSTRING and looking for a 
solution that incorporates that.

(There's nothing wrong with that and it's how we all learn to use code and 
get experience in writing it.)

Sometimes though it can blind us to the essentials of the solution.

If I had really been faced with this problem, my solution would not have 
used UNSTRING (ANY number of them), work fields, or anything else that is 
really extraneous and/or unnecessary.

Here's the solution I actually would have written...(I have included the 
whole thing so it can be easily pasted into an editor and 
compiled/debugged... you and I may not be the only ones following this... 
:-))

000010 IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
000011 PROGRAM-ID.     NVPARMS.
000013 AUTHOR.         PETER E. C. DASHWOOD.
000014 DATE-WRITTEN.   DECEMBER 30TH, 2006.
000015*REMARKS.
000016*
000017*  A SET OF "PARAMETERS" MUST BE PARSED AND PRESENTED TO A
000018*  PROGRAM
000019*  FOR PROCESSING
000020*
000021*  IN FACT, THESE ARE NOT "PARAMETERS" AT ALL BUT ARE REALLY
000022*  AN INPUT
000023*  FILE...
000024*
000025*  NEVERTHELESS THE PROGRAM DEMONSTRATES SOME USES OF:
000026*     UNSTRING
000027*     COMPLEX PERFORM
000028*     COMPLEX INSPECT
000029*
000030*  THE COMPLETE PARAMETER SET IS STORED TO AN ARRAY DURING
000031*  INITIALIZATION AS A 'ONE-TIME' TASK.
000032*
000033*  THIS ARRAY COULD BE VALIDATED DURING INITIALIZATION ALSO,
000034*  AND ENTRIES IN IT CROSS-REFERENCED IF REQUIRED.
000035*
000036*  BY ISOLATING THE CODE TO LOAD THE ARGUMENTS INTO THE
000037*  INITIALIZATION
000038*  PART OF THE PROGRAM, THIS CODE COULD BE USED IN ANY PROGRAM
000039*  THAT HAD A SIMILAR PARAMETER FORMAT. DOING IT FROM THE
000040*  MAINLINE ON A PARAMETER BY PARAMETER BASIS PREVENTS THIS.
000041*
000042
000043 ENVIRONMENT DIVISION.
000044 CONFIGURATION SECTION.
000045 SOURCE-COMPUTER. IBM-PC.
000046 OBJECT-COMPUTER. IBM-PC.
000056 DATA DIVISION.
000057 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
000058 01  ARGUMENTS.
000059     12 NAME-VALUE-PAIR OCCURS 40
000060                        INDEXED BY ARGS-X1.
000061        15 ARG-NAME    PIC X(25).
000062        15 ARG-VALUE   PIC X(25).
000063        15 ARG-EOG     PIC X.  *> INDICATES THAT THIS ENTRY IS
000064                               *> THE END OF A "GROUP" OF
000065                               *> PARAMETERS.
000066
000067           88 ARG-END-OF-GROUP  VALUE '1'.
000068
000069 01  ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT   PIC S9(4) COMP VALUE 40.
000070*> MUST MATCH VALUE IN OCCURS ABOVE.
000072
000080 01  IN-DATA.
000081     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000083     "userId=FJS�location=AURO�function=filmRequest�acct".
000084     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000086     "Number=1234567890�userExtension=1403�routing=branc".
000087     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000089     "h�routeLoc=K-MISS�routeAttn=Joe�comments=Comments ".
000090     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000092     "Go Here�debit�date=121306�amount=100.00�sequenceNb".
000093     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000095     "r=12345678��credit�date=051406�amount=900.00�seque".
000096     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000098     "nceNbr=11122233��ATM�date=010106�amount=123.45��ch".
000099     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000101     "argeback�date=010106�amount=500.00��statement�date".
000102     12 FILLER PIC X(50) VALUE
000104     "=032906�amount=1000.00�                           ".
000105 01  INPUT-DATA REDEFINES IN-DATA PIC X(400).
000106
000112
000113 01  VARIOUS-COUNTS USAGE COMP.
000114     12 MAX-ARGUMENTS    PIC S9(4).
000115     12 INPUT-DATA-POS   PIC S9(4).
000116     12 STRING-PARM-LEN  PIC S9(4).
000117     12 J                PIC S9(4).
000119     12 INPUT-DATA-LENGTH PIC S9(4).
000120     12 NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS PIC S9(4).
000121
000122
000130 01  VARIOUS-OTHER-DATA.
000140     12 INPUT-STRING-ID     PIC X(25).
000150     12 INPUT-STRING-PARM   PIC X(25).
000151     12 NV-WORK             PIC X(60).
000152     12 MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER PIC X VALUE "�".
000153     12 MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR PIC X VALUE "=".
000154
000160 01  FLAGS.
000161     12 FINISH-FLAG         PIC X VALUE SPACE.
000162        88 FINISHED           VALUE '1'.
000163        88 NOT-FINISHED       VALUE '0'.
000164     12 REQUEST-FLAG        PIC X VALUE SPACE.
000165        88 END-OF-REQUEST           VALUE '1'.
000166        88 NOT-END-OF-REQUEST       VALUE '0'.
000167     12 NAME-VALUE-FLAG      PIC X VALUE SPACE.
000168        88 ITSA-NAME           VALUE '1'.
000169        88 ITSA-VALUE          VALUE '0'.
000170
000171
000172
000180 PROCEDURE DIVISION.
000190 MAIN SECTION.
000191 000.
000192     PERFORM 100-INITIAL-SETUP
000193     PERFORM 200-PROCESSING UNTIL FINISHED
000194*     PERFORM 900-CLOSE-DOWN
000195     STOP RUN
000196     .
000197*>===========================================================
000200 100-INITIAL-SETUP SECTION.
000201 110-IS.
000202     SET NOT-FINISHED TO TRUE
000210     PERFORM 2000-LOAD-ARGUMENTS
000220      *> IN THIS SCENARIO THE ARGUMENTS ARE PARSED AND LOADED
000221      *> ONCE
000230      *> DURING INITIALIZATION.
000231      *>
000232      *> IT IS A GENERAL PURPOSE LOAD ROUTINE. (WORKS FOR ANY
000233      *> PROGRAM WITH PARAMETERS IN THE NAME=VALUE FORMAT).
000234      *>
000240      *>
000250      *> ON COMPLETION ALL ARGUMENTS HAVE BEEN LOADED INTO THE
000260      *> "ARGUMENTS" ARRAY. GROUPS OF ARGUMENTS THAT REPRESENT
000261      *> A "RECORD" WILL HAVE THE GROUP FLAG SET IN THE LAST NAME
000262      *> /VALUE PAIR OF THE GROUP
000270      *>
000280      *> INPUT-STRING-ID AND INPUT-STRING-PARM CAN BE LOADED FROM
000281      *> THIS
000290      *> ARRAY USING THE ARGS-X1 INDEX. THIS IS DONE BY PERFORMING
000291      *> 2100-PARSE-INPUT-DATA.
000300      *>
000310     .
000311 199-IS.
000312     EXIT.
000313*>================================================================
000314
000320 200-PROCESSING SECTION.
000321 210-P.
000330     *> VARIOUS PROCESSING OCCURS HERE...
000340
000350     PERFORM 2100-PARSE-INPUT-DATA  *> GET THE NEXT NAME/VALUE
000351                                    *> PAIR
000360
000370     *> PROCESSING CONTINUES....USING INPUT-STRING-ID
000380     *>                           AND INPUT-STRING-PARM
000390     *> AS AT PRESENT.
000391
000400     SET FINISHED TO TRUE
000480     .
000490 299-P.
000500     EXIT.
000561*>==============================================================
000562*>
000563*>          SUBROUTINES ACTIVATED FROM ABOVE...
000564*>
000565*>==============================================================
000566 2000-LOAD-ARGUMENTS     SECTION.
000567 2000-LA-000.
000568     *> THE FOLLOWING CODE PARSES THE NAME/VALUE PAIRS IN
000569     *> INPUT-DATA
000570     *> AND LOADS THEM INTO THE ARGUMENTS ARRAY.
000571     *>
000572     MOVE SPACES TO ARGUMENTS
000573     IF INPUT-DATA (1:1) = MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
000574        MOVE 2 TO INPUT-DATA-POS   *> STEP OVER FIRST FIELD
000575                                   *> DELIMITER
000576                                   *> IF ONE IS PRESENT
000577     ELSE
000578        MOVE 1 TO INPUT-DATA-POS
000579     END-IF
000580     COMPUTE INPUT-DATA-LENGTH = FUNCTION STORED-CHAR-LENGTH
000581                                          (INPUT-DATA)
000582     *> IF YOUR ENVIRONMENT DOESN'T SUPPORT THE ABOVE
000583     *> INTRINSIC FUNCTION, YOU WILL NEED TO ESTABLISH
000584     *> THE TOTAL LENGTH OF THE PARAMETER STRINGS
000585     *> IN "INPUT-DATA" USING "INSPECT" OR ONE OF THE
000586     *> TECHNIQUES DISCUSSED IN CLC
000587     MOVE ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT TO MAX-ARGUMENTS
000588     SET ITSA-NAME TO TRUE
000589     SET ARGS-X1 TO 1
000590     MOVE 1 TO J   *> POINTER USED TO BUILD EACH NAME OR VALUE
000591     PERFORM
000592        VARYING INPUT-DATA-POS
000593           FROM INPUT-DATA-POS
000594             BY 1
000595        UNTIL INPUT-DATA-POS > INPUT-DATA-LENGTH OR
000596              ARGS-X1 > MAX-ARGUMENTS
000598                 EVALUATE  INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1)
000599                    WHEN  MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR
000600                       SET ITSA-VALUE TO TRUE
000601                       MOVE 1 TO J
000602                    WHEN  MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
000603                       SET ITSA-NAME TO TRUE
000604                       IF INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS + 1:1) = 
MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
000605                          SET ARG-END-OF-GROUP (ARGS-X1) TO TRUE
000607                       END-IF
000608                       MOVE 1 TO J
000609                       SET ARGS-X1 UP BY 1
000610                    WHEN OTHER
000611                       IF ITSA-NAME
000612                          MOVE INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) TO 
ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1) (J:1)
000613                          ADD 1 TO J
000614                       ELSE
000615                          MOVE INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) TO 
ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1) (J:1)
000616                          ADD 1 TO J
000617                       END-IF
000618                  END-EVALUATE
000650     END-PERFORM
000651     SET NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS TO ARGS-X1
000652     SUBTRACT 1 FROM NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS
000653     SET ARGS-X1 TO 1 *> SET INDEX FOR USE FROM MAINLINE CODE
000654     SET ARGS-X1 DOWN BY 1
000655     .
000656 2000-LA-999.
000657     EXIT.
000658 *>==============================================================
000659 2100-PARSE-INPUT-DATA     SECTION.
000660 2100-PID-000.
000661 *> THIS CODE LOADS INPUT-STRING-ID AND INPUT-STRING-PARM WITH
000662 *> THE NEXT
000663 *> VALID NAME/VALUE PAIR.
000664 *> IT DOESN'T PARSE THE INPUT-DATA BUT THE EFFECT IS THE SAME AS
000665 *> IF IT HAD...
000666     SET ARGS-X1 UP BY 1
000667     IF  ARGS-X1 NOT > NUMBER-NAME-VALUE-PAIRS
000668         MOVE ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1) TO INPUT-STRING-ID
000669         MOVE ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1) TO INPUT-STRING-PARM
000670         IF ARG-END-OF-GROUP (ARGS-X1)
000671            SET END-OF-REQUEST TO TRUE
000672         ELSE
000673            SET NOT-END-OF-REQUEST TO TRUE
000674         END-IF
000675     ELSE
000676       MOVE SPACE TO INPUT-STRING-ID
000677                     INPUT-STRING-PARM
000678     END-IF
000679     .
000680 2100-PID-999.
000681     EXIT.
000682*>============================ END OF PROGRAM ===================
000870


A few comments about the above...

1. The test for a delimiter at the start could be removed if it is 
absolutely certain that no such delimiter will ever be encountered.
2. If a double delimiter is encountered INPUT-DATA-POS could be incremented 
by 1 to step over it (for  a marginal efficiency gain), but the logic works 
whether you do this or not.
3. The last group of parms will not set the group flag unless they are 
delimited by a double delimiter. It is very easy to change this so that the 
last group is always set as a group by adding 1 line to the code. (Or 
ensuring input is terminated by a double delimiter...)
4. Because of the proportional font used in these messages, the code looks 
pretty awful when posted here. In a proper Editor, properly formatted as 
COBOL source, it looks much better. :-)

This code does exactly what is required with no work areas, no UNSTRINGs, a 
single pass parse of the input data, and also stores the whole parameter set 
as a single, one-time task during initialization. (there are a number of 
advantages in doing this).

HOWEVER, the code requires the input to be in the expected format. It 
doesn't deal with embedded spaces or syntax errors. If I were designing 
this, I would make the parameters free format and remove the delimiter. 
Parameters would ALWAYS be name/value pairs separated by a single equals 
sign. (If you really just want a parm with no value, set the value to 
"dummy" or "present" or some agreed string.) Doing this means the parms can 
be easily entered from a variety of inputs, and they can be checked for 
validity and syntax before having their values validated.

<snip>>
> The thing I like about my original method, other than requiring two
> unstrings, is that no temporary field is required.
>

Don't like work fields? See above... :-)


> Anyway, thanks for giving it a shot!
>

It really was a pleasure, Frank. I'm not saying it is the best solution, but 
it's the best I can do in the time I allotted for this. Hopefully, some 
people will get a few ideas from it... :-)

COBOL is definitely fun to write and I'll miss that aspect of it. Maybe, in 
time, I'll get to feel the same about C#... I like it, it is simple and 
concise, but I'm not facile enough with it yet to really push the envelope. 
I had a major breakthrough with it yesterday when I managed to get it to 
raise an event (when the event hadn't actually occurred) and so save 
duplicating all the code that handled that event... :-) It was quite 
bizarre.. I waded through pages of example code, read a whole lot of stuff 
about raising various kinds of events (none of which were what I actually 
wanted), traced through some very advanced delegation classes until my head 
swum, then a light flashed on ... "Why don't I just..." did it and 
everything worked... with one line of code...:-)

Pete.

Many people would share it. However, I believe that because it is less than 
a dozen lines of code and provided it is commented, most people would see 
what the code is trying to do.

The EVALUATE makes it very clear that if a delimiter is encountered the next 
thing will be a parameter Name and if an = is encountered, what follows will 
be a Value. (If no value is present the delimiter forces a reset back to the 
name). Having the specific relationship between these things automatically 
documented by EVALUATE, I think, is a bonus.

The only "hairy" bit I can see are the two subscripted refmodded lines used 
to build the name and values into the master ARGUMENTS table. Arnold 
commented on this, but agreed he understood how they worked.

Obviously, I think it is OK :-)

>
>>HOWEVER, the code requires the input to be in the expected format. It
…[12 more quoted lines elided]…
> inside of quotes, but we felt this was simpler.

I noted that "this is a comment" had embedded spaces so perhaps the 
delimiters are useful after all... :-)

I see no difference (apart from the character chosen) between having a ' or 
having a |... Are they not logically equivalent in this case?


>The request is always
> generated by a program, so I'm not too worried about how simple it is for 
> a
> user to enter it.
>

Fair enough. Then they can be fixed format...

>>> Anyway, thanks for giving it a shot!
>>>
…[25 more quoted lines elided]…
> often too verbose and is not 'simple and concise'.

add rams to ewes giving lambs.

OR

01 penis size is enormous class is alpha
              usage is internal floating-point.

(Sadly no longer valid, but worked in COBOL 59, so long as 'enormous' was a 
comp item, separately defined, with a value of  4 or 8)


OR

alter points to proceed to head-on-train-wreck

OR

read newspaper, at end set fire to it.

There are some others I can think of but probably not suitable for family 
viewing and, strictly speaking SQL, not COBOL... :-)

…[5 more quoted lines elided]…

"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in message
news:507m66F1e3a49U2@mid.individual.net...

>>> Pete Dashwood<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> 01/02/07 5:19 PM >>>
<SNIP>

>>I noted that "this is a comment" had embedded spaces so perhaps the
>>delimiters are useful after all... :-)
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
>
Ah. I was thinking...

'function=do this'     'name=Frank Swarbrick'

Here's the amended COBOL to do your interpretation...

                EVALUATE  INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1)
                       WHEN  MSG-FIELD-SEPARATOR
000600                       SET ITSA-VALUE TO TRUE
000601                       MOVE 1 TO J

000602           WHEN  MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
000603                   IF INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS + 1:1) = SPACE
                                    SET ITSA-NAME TO TRUE
                                    MOVE 1 TO J
                                    SET ARGS-X1 UP BY 1
                              END-IF
                              IF INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS + 1:1) = 
MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER
000605                          SET ARG-END-OF-GROUP (ARGS-X1) TO TRUE
000607                  END-IF
000608
000609
000610           WHEN OTHER
000611                   IF ITSA-NAME
                                    IF INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) NOT = 
SPACE
000612                             MOVE INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) TO 
ARG-NAME (ARGS-X1) (J:1)
000613                             ADD 1 TO J
                                    END-IF
000614                   ELSE
000615                          MOVE INPUT-DATA (INPUT-DATA-POS:1) TO 
ARG-VALUE (ARGS-X1) (J:1)
000616                          ADD 1 TO J
000617                   END-IF
000618    END-EVALUATE

It took 5 minutes to do this, but I haven't tested it.

NOTE:
1. MSG-FIELD-DELIMITER now has a value of  ' (single quote)
2. Name/value pairs are now free format and can be separated by any number 
of
    spaces (there must be at least 1...).
2. Values cannot start with a space, but may contain embedded spaces...
     name='Frank Swarbrick'  is OK... comment=' some comment here' is NOT OK
     (It would require one more line to make this so that a leading space is 
OK, but then
      name/value pairs would always require at least two spaces separating 
them.)
3. END-OF-GROUP is now detected by two single quotes...''
4. Name/value pairs must have at least one space separating them.

The point about this is that it is pretty easy to amend, but any change in 
the syntax will result in a corresponding change in the 'rules'.

<snip>

>>> To be honest, I often find COBOL the opposite of fun to write, because
> its
…[29 more quoted lines elided]…
> consider COBOL to be one of them.  :-)

Not at all, but I do think (as Mary Poppins observed) a spoonful of sugar

…[15 more quoted lines elided]…

My favourite:

	MOVE SPACE TO MUST-BE-SPACE MUST-NOT-BE-SPACE.
	UNSTRING INPUT-FIELD DELIMITED BY ALL SPACE
		INTO MUST-NOT-BE-SPACE MUST-BE-SPACE.
	IF MUST-BE-SPACE IS NOT EQUAL TO SPACE
		OR
	   MUST-NOT-BE-SPACE IS EQUAL TO SPACE
		DISPLAY "Danger Will Robinson !"
		DISPLAY "Input must contain data with"
		DISPLAY "no embedded spaces!".

"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> schrieb im Newsbeitrag 
news:500b4bF1d47t2U1@mid.individual.net...

> 000057 WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
> 000058 01  ARGUMENTS.
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> 000070*> MUST MATCH VALUE IN OCCURS ABOVE.

This previous comment highlights a problem, that we also encounter 
sometimes: how can we enforce, that the same value/literal is used in 
various places within a program? Assuming that a COBOL compiler supporting 
the REPLACE statement is available, we found a solution, that could be 
applied to the example above like this:

     REPLACE  ==a-t-l== BY ==40==.
     ....
     ....
         12 NAME-VALUE-PAIR OCCURS a-t-l
     ....
     01  ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT  PIC S9(4) COMP VALUE a-t-l.
     ....

Are there any experiences with such an approach?
Any pro and con arguments would be welcome.

Karl Kiesel
Fujitsu Siemens Computers, M�nchen

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Productivity

_(thread depth: 17)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2007-01-06T00:43:21+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<506ruoF1ehb1uU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4v33ipF1a006cU1@mid.individual.net> <12oosqtmgaqcd81@news.supernews.com> <4v7ajgF1bf6u8U1@mid.individual.net> <1166980834.471149.102990@i12g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <4v8qu1F1b75r0U1@mid.individual.net> <dElkh.4094$yx6.3439@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net> <4vf0t1F1bfj5nU1@mid.individual.net> <4vfl66F1as7a4U1@mid.individual.net> <4vgj6mF1a4g7nU1@mid.individual.net> <4vimr5F1cedo7U1@mid.individual.net> <4vj2kkF1co1akU1@mid.individual.net> <4vlbkiF1bf56sU1@mid.individual.net> <4vlnqgF1c247oU1@mid.individual.net> <4vm6ldF16ggd7U1@mid.individual.net> <4vvj6rF1dqm00U1@mid.individual.net> <500b4bF1d47t2U1@mid.individual.net> <enl1cs$4lg$1@nntp.fujitsu-siemens.com>`

```

"Karl Kiesel" <Karl.Kiesel@fujitsu-siemens.com> wrote in message 
news:enl1cs$4lg$1@nntp.fujitsu-siemens.com...
>
> "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> schrieb im 
…[30 more quoted lines elided]…
>
This is the most imaginative use of COPY I have ever seen :-)

Full marks for imagination and thinking "outside the square".

I've never seen this before and I am blown away by the idea of it.

However, I probably won't use it :-).

These are all personal opinions and there is no reason why people (who don't 
have my prejudices) shouldn't use this approach. Here's why I personally 
will not adopt it:

1. I HATE using COBOL COPY. If it is source code for a frequently used 
routine, I  simply write a subprogram (or subClass). If it is source for a 
file definition or working-storage record layout, I don't use the COBOL file 
system so I don't need them. (I have been known to create a COPY block for 
SQL Host variables, but this does not require REPLACING, as the names are 
DECLGENed and only used in one place in the program. (Within an SQL DECLARE 
block...) It requires a DECLGEN if the database changes, and then the 
DECLGEN has to be applied to the COPY block, and all the programs that use 
the COPY block must be recompiled... too much like hard work.)  Eventually I 
realised that a separation layer made the whole thing much simpler and that 
is what I use currently. My application programs don't contain ESQL any 
more. They call an interface. As I move off COBOL this becomes even simpler 
with immediate result sets returned and manipulated offline. I'm liking this 
approach more and more. Things like Data Adapters, Table Adapters and 
Readers in C# make ESQL look Stone Age. Why open a cursor and maintain a DB 
connection so you can run it, when you can run it offline...? Sure, the 
programs require SQL strings to tell them what to get, but they don't need 
to hold a DB Connection once they have got it.

(If you are working in an environment where they use high-powered tools like 
ENDEVOR, which are designed specifically for source management, it isn't so 
bad, but if you have to manage it yourself it becomes a nightmare. Never 
mind source code management, I had to write my own DECLGEN for the PC, 
because there isn't one in the environment I work with. I'm not planning on 
writing ENDEVOR any time soon... :-))

2. I don't need or want to maintain COBOL source,  and using COPY just 
perpetuates this.

3. I can see the above solution becoming confusing if there are a number of 
variables being maintained by it, but I expect this could be managed by 
using suitable COPY Names.

4. If the variable is maintained within the program, close to whatever it 
applies to, it is easy for a Programmer to check the value. If an external 
source has to be updated in isolation, I see this as a potential source of 
error ( for example, using the example cited...Two things are being updated 
in two places; the OCCURS value on the table, and a separate field that 
reflects the limit on the array. Using the proposed approach these two 
things must be updated in two separate places (The OCCURS in the source 
program and the limit in the COPY book.) Provided changes are only made 
rarely it is a good way to ensure the value of the limit variable, but so is 
coding it as a VALUE within the program... :-) Bottom line: For this type of 
instance, it probably isn't much help.

Having said all of that, I can see cases where the suggested approach WOULD 
be very viable. For independent variables in WS, where the said variable is 
defined in many programs, this would be a very good way to administer the 
value of the variable from a single central point.

Thanks, Karl, for a really imaginative and thought-provoking use of 
COPY...REPLACING.

Pete.

Pete





> Are there any experiences with such an approach?
> Any pro and con arguments would be welcome.
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Productivity

- **From:** "Rick Smith" <ricksmith@mfi.net>

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<12psg05ovqubv16@corp.supernews.com>`

```
Pete Dashwood<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> 01/05/07 4:43 AM >>>
>
>1. I HATE using COBOL COPY. If it is source code for a frequently used 
>routine, I  simply write a subprogram (or subClass). If it is source for a

>file definition or working-storage record layout, I don't use the COBOL
file 
>system so I don't need them. (I have been known to create a COPY block for

>SQL Host variables, but this does not require REPLACING, as the names are 
>DECLGENed and only used in one place in the program. (Within an SQL DECLARE

>block...) It requires a DECLGEN if the database changes, and then the 
>DECLGEN has to be applied to the COPY block, and all the programs that use

>the COPY block must be recompiled... too much like hard work.)  Eventually
I 
>realised that a separation layer made the whole thing much simpler and that

>is what I use currently. My application programs don't contain ESQL any 
>more. They call an interface. As I move off COBOL this becomes even simpler

>with immediate result sets returned and manipulated offline. I'm liking
this 
>approach more and more. Things like Data Adapters, Table Adapters and 
>Readers in C# make ESQL look Stone Age. Why open a cursor and maintain a DB

>connection so you can run it, when you can run it offline...? Sure, the 
>programs require SQL strings to tell them what to get, but they don't need

>to hold a DB Connection once they have got it.

A few comments...

One, how do you keep your linkage areas in sync without using copybooks? 
Take the following production code:

     MOVE GENERIC-ACCT-SUBR      TO SUBROUTINE         
     CALL SUBROUTINE USING       GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT    
                                 GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT   
                                 GENERIC-ACCT-ERROR    
                                 PSB-PCB-INFO          
                                 ADDRESS OF PCB-PTR-TBL
     ON EXCEPTION                                      
         GO TO 9850-COBOL-ERROR                        
     END-CALL                                          

GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT is defined in a copybook called "GENACCTI".
GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT is defined in a copybook called "GENACCTO".
etc.

GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT has twelve distinict input fields.  GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT
has over thirty output (result) fields.  This would be a nightmare without
the copybooks.

Question about your comment about 'intermediate result sets' being
manipulated offline...  This sounds good in theory, and I'm sure it works
most of the time, but I imagine it would not be a good thing if your select
returned hundreds of thousands of rows.  Would you agree?  I guess I'm still
thinking in my "batch processing" mindset, so perhaps that's something you
would simply never need to do.

Frank




--- 
Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA
```

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Productivity

- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<5085fhF1equqlU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4v33ipF1a006cU1@mid.individual.net> <12oosqtmgaqcd81@news.supernews.com> <4v7ajgF1bf6u8U1@mid.individual.net> <1166980834.471149.102990@i12g2000cwa.googlegroups.com> <4v8qu1F1b75r0U1@mid.individual.net> <dElkh.4094$yx6.3439@newsread2.news.pas.earthlink.net> <4vf0t1F1bfj5nU1@mid.individual.net> <4vfl66F1as7a4U1@mid.individual.net> <4vgj6mF1a4g7nU1@mid.individual.net> <4vimr5F1cedo7U1@mid.individual.net> <4vj2kkF1co1akU1@mid.individual.net> <4vlbkiF1bf56sU1@mid.individual.net> <4vlnqgF1c247oU1@mid.individual.net> <4vm6ldF16ggd7U1@mid.individual.net> <4vvj6rF1dqm00U1@mid.individual.net> <500b4bF1d47t2U1@mid.individual.net> <enl1cs$4lg$1@nntp.fujitsu-siemens.com> <506ruoF1ehb1uU1@mid.individual.net> <507nhmF1f24rfU1@mid.individual.net>`

```

"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in message 
news:507nhmF1f24rfU1@mid.individual.net...
> Pete Dashwood<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> 01/05/07 4:43 AM >>>
>>
…[55 more quoted lines elided]…
> the copybooks.

Sure. But I wouldn't be calling SUBROUTINE with parameters.

It would be a Class and GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT would be a set of properties, as 
would GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT. There is then no requirement for the linkage to 
be "in sync", because there is no linkage.

You could still use COPY to define these areas in the calling program if you 
wanted to, but the object properties would simply be an interface block 
large enough to accommodate both of GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT and 
GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT (plus the other two parameters you pass currently. (I'd 
put these at the "top" of the interface block, along with a return code and 
error message. Fixed fields that will not change...)).
...
invoke
   objSubroutine "SET-interface"
         using interface-block
end-invoke
invoke
     objSubroutine "AnyMethod" *> method to manipulate properties as 
currently defined
end-invoke
invoke objSubroutine "GET-interface-block"
     returning interface-block
end-invoke
...

Now a new-field gets added to GENERIC-ACCT-INPUT and a couple of new fields 
are added to GENERIC-ACCT-OUTPUT...

You could override the existing Method or extend it to a new method or use a 
different interface, there are a number of options.

You'd probably take this decision based on how many existing programs are 
affected by the changes.

If they all are, then the Class could be amended to reflect the new 
interface (although I prefer not to do this, personally...)

Now your amendments in the application programs focus on how the new fields 
get used; the code to invoke Subroutine doesn't change, and there is no 
requirement for parameter lists or linkage syncing.

If only some of the apps are affected by the new fields, I'd  probably add a 
new method (maybe inheriting from/ extending the old one...) that recognises 
the interface change.

All of the programs that DON'T use the new stuff will function as they 
always have, without change. I don't believe they require regression 
testing, but it is arguable, depending on the circumstances and the 
interactions between the apps. (If COPY Books are used, everything requires 
regression testing because even programs that don't use the new fields have 
had their interface changed).

I am trying to demonstrate a concept here, it is not a perfect example.

Conceptually, a called subroutine with a parameter list is like a Class with 
a single static interface. The OO approach allows a separation between the 
behaviours (Methods) and the interfaces to them, which cannot be easily 
achieved with procedural programming.

>
> Question about your comment about 'intermediate result sets' being
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
> returned hundreds of thousands of rows.  Would you agree?

I'm not sure. It really depends on the environment you are working in, I 
think.

>I guess I'm still
> thinking in my "batch processing" mindset, so perhaps that's something you
> would simply never need to do.

Certainly, the transactional approach would reduce the size of result 
sets... :-)

Pete.
```

invoke GenAcct 'setBank'(bank-nbr)

I considered using properties instead of methods, but the requirement to
declare them in the repository makes that, umm, inconvenient, especially
when there are dozens or even hundreds of them.  A shame, because it looks
to be a nice feature.  Micro Focus allows you to use the "inline invocation
operator" to access properties, like so:

move bank-nbr to GenAcct::"bank"
*> or
set GenAcct::"bank" to bank-nbr

Which is pretty nice, though it does make it hard to tell the difference
between a property and a method with no parameters (which is why I use empty
pararentheses for the latter; when I remember to do so!).

>they might be a bit less ready to throw the baby out with the bath-water 
>when the time comes to replace systems. I shouldn't think there is anything

>to lose...

Oh, I'm quite sure that MF would be more than willing.  Of course, going
with MF for COBOL would require moving off the mainframe for deployment, and
I just don't think that's going to happen.

Now if MF would port their compiler to VSE, that would be great!  :-)  But
since much (most?) of their business is 'mainframe migration', I don't
forsee that happening.

>> I considered using properties instead of methods, but the requirement to
>> declare them in the repository makes that, umm, inconvenient, especially
>> when there are dozens or even hundreds of them.
>
>No more so than having to declare things in Working-Storage... :-)

But the properties have already been declared in their corresponding
class(es).  Why should I declare them twice?!?  Of course this is where a
copybook might come in handy.  :-)

>A shame, because it looks
>> to be a nice feature.  Micro Focus allows you to use the "inline 
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>I believe Fujitsu also supports it, although I don't use it myself. (Only
on 
>aesthetic grounds...it just doesn't look like COBOL to me, but I realise 
>that s a very empty objection :-))

Well, I often wish that COBOL didn't look quite as much like COBOL as it
does.  Many languages are criticized as being "write once/read never". 
Cobol, in my opinion, goes too far in the other direction.  Is easy to read,
but often a pain to write!  (Simply being too verbose).

In my real life Cobol life we tend to have things like...

01  AGN-A-GROUP-NAME.
    05  AGN-TYPE                   PIC X.
    05  AGN-BALANCE                PIC S9(9)V99 COMP-3.

01  RPT2-IN-DTL1.
    05  RPT2-IN-DTL1-TYPE          PIC X.
    05  RPT2-IN-DTL1-BAL           PIC ZZZ,ZZZ,ZZ9.99+.

    MOVE AGN-TYPE TO RPT2-IN-DTL1-TYPE
    MOVE AGN-BALANCE TO RPT2-IN-DTL1-BAL

Conceivably we could instead do something like this:
01  GROUP-NAME.
    05  TYPE                       PIC X.
    05  BALANCE                    PIC S9(9)V99 COMP-3.

01  RPT2-IN-DTL1.
    05  TYPE                       PIC X.
    05  BALANCE                    PIC ZZZ,ZZZ,ZZ9.99+.

    MOVE TYPE OF AGN-A-GROUP-NAME TO TYPE OF RPT2-IN-DTL1
    MOVE BALANCE OF AGN-A-GROUP-NAME TO BALANCE OF RPT2-IN-DTL1

But that is just not something that anyone here does.  (And yes, in this
case we could have even used MOVE CORR, but generally that probably wouldn't
work.)

I wouldn't say there's a shop standard that's against it.  Just that no one
uses it, and most likely no one sees any reason to use it.  I don't.  It's
too verbose.

Personally, I'd like to see something like this:

01  AGN-A-GROUP-NAME PREFIX AGN.
    05  TYPE                       PIC X.
    05  BALANCE                    PIC S9(9)V99 COMP-3.

01  RPT2-IN-DTL1 PREFIX R2I-DTL1.
    05  TYPE                       PIC X.
    05  BAL                        PIC ZZZ,ZZZ,ZZ9.99+.

    MOVE AGN.TYPE TO R2I-DTL1.TYPE
    MOVE AGN.BALANCE TO R2I-DTL1.BAL

Maybe using ':' as the delimiter, instead of '.', since '.' has other
meanings.
    MOVE AGN:TYPE TO R2I-DTL1:TYPE
    MOVE AGN:BALANCE TO R2I-DTL1:BAL

Or maybe '::', since that's already in "standard COBOL"
    MOVE AGN::TYPE TO R2I-DTL1::TYPE
    MOVE AGN::BALANCE TO R2I-DTL1::BAL

And how about with TYPEDEFs?  I was looking forward to having TYPEDEFs until
I realized it would require me to use the 'OF' clause way too often.

How about:
01  TRANSACTION TYPEDEF.
    05  ACCT-NBR                   PIC 9(10).
    05  TYPE                       PIC X.
    05  AMOUNT                     PIC S9(9)V99 COMP-3.

01  PREV-TRAN                      TYPE TRANSACTION.
01  TRAN                           TYPE TRANSACTION.

IF TRAN.ACCT-NBR = PREV-TRAN.ACCT-NBR
    CONTINUE
ELSE
    PERFORM ACCT-BREAK
    MOVE TRAN TO PREV.TRAN
    MOVE ZERO TO TOTAL-TRAN-AMOUNT
END-IF
ADD TRAN.AMOUNT TO TOTAL-TRAN-AMOUNT

Just thoughts on what I might do if I were in charge of such things.  :-)

Frank


--- 
Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA
```

"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in message 
news:50fnlaF1esfutU1@mid.individual.net...
> Pete Dashwood<dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> 01/05/07 8:41 PM >>>
>>
…[74 more quoted lines elided]…
> I just don't think that's going to happen.

What about using MF for development and deploying to the mainframe? MF have 
some great support tools in this area.
>
> Now if MF would port their compiler to VSE, that would be great!  :-)  But
…[11 more quoted lines elided]…
> copybook might come in handy.  :-)

I don't know about DotNET COBOL, but if a property is declared PUBLIC STATIC 
in a Class, you don't need todeclare it again anywhere. You don't even need 
to instantiate the Class it is defined in, in order to use it.

Quick C# example...

Form1 is a Class and has (among others) a Public Static property declared 
thus:

public partial class Form1 : Form
{
     private static string _DBname;
     // A read-write property that holds a DB path or ODBC system DSN after 
selection by the User
      public static string DBName
     {
      get
     {
      return _DBname;
     }
     set
     {
     _DBname = value;
     }
}

In another Class (Form2 - but it could be any Class...) I need to build a 
connection string for this DB. It is NOT defined anywhere in the current 
Class (Form2). I can create an Object Reference to it (for example - in 
fact, I can do anything I like with it...) as:

object objDBName = Form1.DBName;

The get method for the property is automatically invoked and the private 
_DBName variable form Form1 has its contents returned.

If I removed STATIC from the definition, I would then need an object 
reference pointing to an instance of  Form1 to be established before I could 
reference the property.

This is very useful and has saved my bacon on a few occasions while 
programming in C# :-)

I'm not sure what the equivalent would be in DotNET COBOL, but it would 
probably use the Repository. I'm not keen on using the repository because I 
only ever late bind when using OO COBOL, so I only make Repository entries 
when the program can't compile without them. Fujitsu NetCOBOL (which is an 
OO implemention but does not implement the DotNET Framework) allows 
prototyping of interfaces to be done and this might be another approach to 
the problem of not wanting thngs multiply defined.

>
>>A shame, because it looks
…[75 more quoted lines elided]…
>    MOVE AGN::BALANCE TO R2I-DTL1::BAL

I see little advantage in this, over what you originally coded :-)

>
> And how about with TYPEDEFs?  I was looking forward to having TYPEDEFs 
> until
> I realized it would require me to use the 'OF' clause way too often.
>

Yes, I agree in principle that COBOL could use SOME  kind of shorthand to 
replace 'OF' and 'IN' for qualification.

I suppose you could argue that OF and IN are only 2 characters (4 if you 
count spaces) and, in COBOL terms that shouldn't be onerous.

But I think they look ugly as well... :-)

> How about:
> 01  TRANSACTION TYPEDEF.
…[17 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Hopefully you'd allow negated conditions to be used, instead of that awful 
CONTINUE ? :-)

Pete.

```
"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message 
news:50gagoF1g0uboU1@mid.individual.net...
>
> I don't know about DotNET COBOL, but if a property is declared PUBLIC 
> STATIC in a Class, you don't need todeclare it again anywhere. You don't 
> even need to instantiate the Class it is defined in, in order to use it.

    Just as a heads up, different languages which target the .NET platform 
may assign different semantics or meaning to the same keyword. For example, 
in C#, the "static" keyword does what you claim it does, but in VB.NET, 
static does something completely different. To declare a field which exists 
at the class level, instead of at the instance level, you use the "Shared" 
keyword in VB.NET.

    In other words, the "public static" concept is a C# one (and Java uses a 
similar concept -- not sure if Cobol.NET uses a similar one), not a .NET 
concept.

    - Oliver
```

>OO implemention but does not implement the DotNET Framework) allows 
>prototyping of interfaces to be done and this might be another approach to

>the problem of not wanting thngs multiply defined.

I'm not sure we are on the same page here.  Take the following...

public class Class1
{
    private int myInt;
    public int MyString
    {
        get
        {
            return myInt;
        }
        set
        {
            myInt = value
        }
}

public class MainClass
{
    public static void Main( string[] args )
    {
        Class1 myClass = new Class1;
        myClass.MyInt = 25;
        System.Console.WriteLine(myClass.MyInt);
    }
}

In "standard" OO COBOL you might have something like:

class-id. Class1 as "Class1".
    object.
        data division.
        working-storage section.
        77  my-int    binary-long property.
    end object.
end class Class1.

program-id. Main.
repository.
    class Class1 as "Class1"
    property my-int
    .
data division.
working-storage section.
77  myClass object reference Class1.
procedure division.
    set myClass to Class1::"New"()
    move 25 to my-int of myClass
    display my-int of myClass
    exit program.
end program Main.

I had to define my-int in Class1, and then declare it in the repository of
Main, even though I declared the entire class Class1 in Main.  I'm not sure
why there is a need to declare properties in the repository.  Seems to me
the compiler should be able to read the external repository and see that
my-int is a property of myClass.

Anyway, MF COBOL does allow this if you use the property in a manner similar
to the inline invocation, eg:

program-id. Main.
repository.
    class Class1 as "Class1"
    .
data division.
working-storage section.
77  myClass object reference Class1.
procedure division.
    set myClass to Class1::"New"()
    move 25 to myClass::"my-int"
    display myClass::"my-int"
    exit program.
end program Main.

Doing it this way there is no need to have the 'property my-int' declaration
in the repository.  Seems like a small thing in this example, since there's
only one property, but imagine 100 properties!

I'm guessing the reason has something to do with my-int being a data-name in
the first example and a literal in the second.  Seems an odd distincition,
but I am not a compiler writer, so there may be some justification I don't
know about.  Still doesn't make me like it any more, though!  :-)

>> In my real life Cobol life we tend to have things like...
>>
…[30 more quoted lines elided]…
>> uses it, and most likely no one sees any reason to use it.  I don't. 
It's
>> too verbose.
>>
…[22 more quoted lines elided]…
>I see little advantage in this, over what you originally coded :-)


The point, as little as it may be, is that the sub-level fields (05, etc.)
need not be declared with the entire name.  IE, TYPE vs AGN-TYPE.  (I just
realized that TYPE is a reserved word, but...)  A small thing?  Certainly. 
But I would find it nice.  After all, I'm only dreaming here.

>> And how about with TYPEDEFs?  I was looking forward to having TYPEDEFs 
>> until
…[9 more quoted lines elided]…
>But I think they look ugly as well... :-)

It's ugly and, to me, a bit backwards.  Current: AGN-BALANCE.  With typedef:
BALANCE OF AGN.  Backwards!  :-)  My way: AGN.BALANCE.  Better!  :-)

>> How about:
>> 01  TRANSACTION TYPEDEF.
…[16 more quoted lines elided]…
>> Just thoughts on what I might do if I were in charge of such things. 
:-)
>>
>
>Hopefully you'd allow negated conditions to be used, instead of that awful

>CONTINUE ? :-)

Sure, why not.  :-)  I've had it beaten into me to avoid negated conditions.
 But if they are simple enough (such as in this case) I'm not really against
them.

Frank

```

"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in message
news:50fnlaF1esfutU1@mid.individual.net...
[snip]
> And how about with TYPEDEFs?  I was looking forward to having TYPEDEFs
until
> I realized it would require me to use the 'OF' clause way too often.

It may be possible to avoid using OF (or IN) by using
the 66 RENAMES.

> How about:
> 01  TRANSACTION TYPEDEF.
>     05  ACCT-NBR                   PIC 9(10).
>     05  TYPE                       PIC X.
Change to TYP since TYPE is a reserved word.
>     05  AMOUNT                     PIC S9(9)V99 COMP-3.
>
> 01  PREV-TRAN                      TYPE TRANSACTION.
        66 PREV-TRAN-ACCT-NBR RENAMES ACCT-NBR.
        66 PREV-TRAN-TYP RENAMES TYP.
        66 PREV-TRAN-AMOUNT RENAMES AMOUNT.
> 01  TRAN                           TYPE TRANSACTION.
        66 TRAN-ACCT-NBR RENAMES ACCT-NBR.
        66 TRAN-TYP RENAMES TYP.
        66 TRAN-AMOUNT RENAMES AMOUNT.

Replace the "." separator with "-" in the following.

> IF TRAN.ACCT-NBR = PREV-TRAN.ACCT-NBR
>     CONTINUE
…[7 more quoted lines elided]…
> Just thoughts on what I might do if I were in charge of such things.  :-)

However 66 RENAMES can not be used with entries
subordinate to an OCCURS clause or an 88 condition-name.

TYPEDEFs may be used to maintain consistent USAGE
and PICTURE, yet, with 66 RENAMES, allow most
procedure division statements to avoid the use of OF or IN.

[I checked the above statements using Micro Focus 3.2.24
(where TYPEDEF is an extension) and by reading the FDIS
for COBOL 2002.]
```

"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in message
news:50ki2hF1g4q80U1@mid.individual.net...
> >
> >
…[53 more quoted lines elided]…
> Even more typing!  Thanks, but no.  :-)

I do not understand!

TYPEDEF saves several hundred (maybe a few thousand)
characters. OF (or IN) adds a few hundred to several hundred
characters. Judicious use of RENAMES adds a few hundred;
but saves a few hundred to several hundred characters by
avoiding OF (or IN). [Depending on the program.]

The key, it seems, is that, where the judicious use of RENAMES
adds fewer characters than are saved by using TYPEDEF, the
result will be less typing. Therefore, I do not understand how
less typing would be "Even more typing!".

Perhaps you could explain your comment.
```

```
Rick Smith<ricksmith@mfi.net> 01/10/07 12:45 PM >>>
>
>"Frank Swarbrick" <Frank.Swarbrick@efirstbank.com> wrote in message
…[8 more quoted lines elided]…
>> >> And how about with TYPEDEFs?  I was looking forward to having
TYPEDEFs
>> >until
>> >> I realized it would require me to use the 'OF' clause way too often.
…[60 more quoted lines elided]…
>Perhaps you could explain your comment.

I think we may be on two different pages.  I was comparing yours:

01  TRANSACTION TYPEDEF.
    05  ACCT-NBR                   PIC 9(10).
    05  TYP                        PIC X.
    05  AMOUNT                     PIC S9(9)V99 COMP-3.

01  PREV-TRAN                      TYPE TRANSACTION.
    66 PREV-TRAN-ACCT-NBR RENAMES ACCT-NBR.
    66 PREV-TRAN-TYP RENAMES TYP.
    66 PREV-TRAN-AMOUNT RENAMES AMOUNT.

01  TRAN                           TYPE TRANSACTION.
    66 TRAN-ACCT-NBR RENAMES ACCT-NBR.
    66 TRAN-TYP RENAMES TYP.
    66 TRAN-AMOUNT RENAMES AMOUNT.

IF TRAN-ACCT-NBR = PREV-TRAN-ACCT-NBR
    CONTINUE
ELSE
    PERFORM ACCT-BREAK
    MOVE TRAN TO PREV-TRAN
    MOVE ZERO TO TOTAL-TRAN-AMOUNT
END-IF
ADD TRAN-AMOUNT TO TOTAL-TRAN-AMOUNT

With my "pseudo-COBOL" version.

01  TRANSACTION TYPEDEF.
    05  ACCT-NBR                   PIC 9(10).
    05  TYP                        PIC X.
    05  AMOUNT                     PIC S9(9)V99 COMP-3.

01  PREV-TRAN                      TYPE TRANSACTION.
01  TRAN                           TYPE TRANSACTION.

IF TRAN.ACCT-NBR = PREV-TRAN.ACCT-NBR
    CONTINUE
ELSE
    PERFORM ACCT-BREAK
    MOVE TRAN TO PREV.TRAN
    MOVE ZERO TO TOTAL-TRAN-AMOUNT
END-IF
ADD TRAN.AMOUNT TO TOTAL-TRAN-AMOUNT

Whereas I think you must have been comparing yours versus a version not
using TYPEDEF.

Or were you comparing it to this?
01  TRANSACTION TYPEDEF.
    05  ACCT-NBR                   PIC 9(10).
    05  TYP                        PIC X.
    05  AMOUNT                     PIC S9(9)V99 COMP-3.

01  PREV-TRAN                      TYPE TRANSACTION.
01  TRAN                           TYPE TRANSACTION.

IF ACCT-NBR OF TRAN = ACCT-NBR OF PREV-TRAN
    CONTINUE
ELSE
    PERFORM ACCT-BREAK
    MOVE TRAN TO PREV-TRAN
    MOVE ZERO TO TOTAL-TRAN-AMOUNT
END-IF
ADD AMOUNT OF TRAN TO TOTAL-TRAN-AMOUNT

Even that version is less typing than your version.

What I was saying is that, you are typing "ALT-FIELD-NAME RENAMES
FIELD-NAME" in order to be able to say "MOVE ALT-FIELD-NAME TO ..." instead
of "MOVE FIELD-NAME OF XXX TO...".  It looks like more typing to me.

I'm probably just not understanding what you are getting at.

Frank




--- 
Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA
```

Assuming TYPEDEF is used, then with regard to typing,
the total number of characters that will be used depends
upon the frequency of reference in a complete program;
not in code used as an example. If it is correctly anticipated
that qualification will be used frequently with particular
data-names and those data-names are renamed, there
will be less typing. I hope that is clear. <g>

   Just wanted to make certain that those thinking about using the ISO 2002 
enhancement of "TYPEDEFs" also look at the implications of "strong" and "weak"

```

"Karl Kiesel" <Karl.Kiesel@fujitsu-siemens.com> wrote in message
news:enl1cs$4lg$1@nntp.fujitsu-siemens.com...
>
> "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> schrieb im
Newsbeitrag
> news:500b4bF1d47t2U1@mid.individual.net...
>
…[30 more quoted lines elided]…
> Any pro and con arguments would be welcome.

I find the REPLACE statement in COBOL 85 to be
too limiting since only one REPLACE statement may
be in effect at one time. [This has been corrected in
the 2002 COBOL standard.] Because I use a COBOL
85 system, I tend to use extensions to overcome those
limitations. However, with COBOL 85 conforming
code, there may be a more interesting approach.

If ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT is used only as a sending
field (it is, in the program presented), then the following
may be preferred.

Insert, at the beginning of working-storage, ...

REPLACE ==ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT== BY ==40==.

Change, ...

000059     12 NAME-VALUE-PAIR OCCURS 40
000060                        INDEXED BY ARGS-X1.

To, ...

000059     12 NAME-VALUE-PAIR OCCURS ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT
000060                        INDEXED BY ARGS-X1.

Remove the statement and comment, ...

000069 01  ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT   PIC S9(4) COMP VALUE 40.
000070*> MUST MATCH VALUE IN OCCURS ABOVE.

In the procedure division, the statement, ...

000587     MOVE ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT TO MAX-ARGUMENTS

After the REPLACE statement, will become, ...

000587     MOVE 40 TO MAX-ARGUMENTS

When moving to COBOL 2002, the above REPLACE
statement may be changed to, ...

01 ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT CONSTANT 40.

Alternatively, one may simply force the correct value,
at the beginning of the program, with the statement, ...

COMPUTE ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT =
    FUNCTION LENGTH (ARGUMENTS)
        / FUNCTION LENGTH (NAME-VALUE-PAIR)

Or, similarly, test the value and issue an error message
if it is not correct.
```

```
Very interesting stuff, Rick.

I like the constant and the calculation using functions best.

I would use the function calculation during initialization, but I'd add a 
comment to it.

Although it deals very nicely with changes to the number of entries, it is 
not as immediately intuitive as a straightforward

MOVE 40 TO ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT

Nevertheless, I really like the function solution and would certainly use 
it.

```
Rick Smith<ricksmith@mfi.net> 01/05/07 5:03 AM >>>
>
>"Karl Kiesel" <Karl.Kiesel@fujitsu-siemens.com> wrote in message
…[23 more quoted lines elided]…
>> various places within a program? Assuming that a COBOL compiler
supporting
>> the REPLACE statement is available, we found a solution, that could be
>> applied to the example above like this:
…[18 more quoted lines elided]…
>code, there may be a more interesting approach.

Yes, but a REPLACE statement can have multiple replaces within it.  Here's
some production code as an example:

REPLACE
   ==:PCB-CNT:== BY ==2==  
   ==:CNA:== BY ==GAI-CNA==
   ==:NPP:== BY ==3==
   ==:LPN:== BY ==22==
   ==:CTR-CNT:== BY ==39==
.

     05  NOTICES-PER-PAGE        PIC S9(3) COMP-3 VALUE :NPP:.

 01  NOTICE-LINE-TABLE.                             
     05                          OCCURS :NPP: TIMES.
         10  NOTICE-LINE         OCCURS :LPN: TIMES.
             15  NL-CC           PIC X.             
             15  NL-LINE         PIC X(79).         

 01  PCB-PTR-TBL.                                      
     05  PCB-PTR                 OCCURS :PCB-CNT: TIMES
                                 POINTER.              


         SET CTR-IDX TO :CTR-CNT:

     SET CTR-MAX TO :CTR-CNT:


>If ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT is used only as a sending
>field (it is, in the program presented), then the following
…[27 more quoted lines elided]…
>000587     MOVE 40 TO MAX-ARGUMENTS

True enough!

>When moving to COBOL 2002, the above REPLACE
>statement may be changed to, ...
>
>01 ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT CONSTANT 40.

Cool.

>Alternatively, one may simply force the correct value,
>at the beginning of the program, with the statement, ...
…[3 more quoted lines elided]…
>        / FUNCTION LENGTH (NAME-VALUE-PAIR)

This won't allow you to use ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT in the occurs clause.

>Or, similarly, test the value and issue an error message
>if it is not correct.

Do you mean something like:
IF ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT NOT EQUAL TO (FUNCTION LENGTH(ARGUMENTS) / FUNCTION
LENGTH(NAME-VALUE-PAIR)
    ...do error message here...
END-IF
?

I don't think this because it always gives a compiler warning that the
statement will never be executed.  (I don't like superfulous warnings, if I
can avoid them.)

Frank

Frank Swarbrick
Senior Developer/Analyst - Mainframe Applications
FirstBank Data Corporation - Lakewood, CO  USA

I never contended otherwise, Mr Swarbrick. Any person
examining the general format for the REPLACE
statement could determine as much from the elipsis at the
end of the format.

[snip]
> >Alternatively, one may simply force the correct value,
> >at the beginning of the program, with the statement, ...
…[5 more quoted lines elided]…
> This won't allow you to use ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT in the occurs clause.

My use of "Alternatively" was intended to convey that
there would be no change to the OCCURS clause, then
the above statement would place the correct value into
ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT without regard to its VALUE
clause.

> >Or, similarly, test the value and issue an error message
> >if it is not correct.
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> ?

Yes, except an additional parenthesis at the end.
... NAME-VALUE-PAIR))

> I don't think this because it always gives a compiler warning that the
> statement will never be executed.  (I don't like superfulous warnings, if
I
> can avoid them.)

           IF ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT NOT EQUAL TO
               (FUNCTION LENGTH (ARGUMENTS)
                   / FUNCTION LENGTH (NAME-VALUE-PAIR))
               DISPLAY QUOTE "ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT" QUOTE
                   SPACE "HAS INCORRECT VALUE"
           END-IF

I entered the above code into the program and changed
the VALUE clause for ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT to +0 to
make certain it would be incorrect. After checking and
running the code, the following message appeared on
the display.

"ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT" HAS INCORRECT VALUE

I then restored the value 40, checked, and ran the program.
No message was displayed.

I am certain that the comparison works correctly, on a
conforming compiler, with no warnings or other errors.

I reduced to program NVPAMS to its minimum and
renamed it as included here.

       IDENTIFICATION DIVISION.
       PROGRAM-ID.     NVTEST.
       DATA DIVISION.
       WORKING-STORAGE SECTION.
       01  ARGUMENTS.
           12 NAME-VALUE-PAIR OCCURS 40
                        INDEXED BY ARGS-X1.
               15 ARG-NAME    PIC X(25).
               15 ARG-VALUE   PIC X(25).
               15 ARG-EOG     PIC X.  *> INDICATES THAT THIS ENTRY IS
                               *> THE END OF A "GROUP" OF
                               *> PARAMETERS.

                   88 ARG-END-OF-GROUP  VALUE "1".

       01  ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT   PIC S9(4) COMP VALUE +0.
       *> MUST MATCH VALUE IN OCCURS ABOVE.

       PROCEDURE DIVISION.
       MAIN SECTION.
       000.
           IF ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT NOT EQUAL TO
               (FUNCTION LENGTH (ARGUMENTS)
                   / FUNCTION LENGTH (NAME-VALUE-PAIR))
               DISPLAY QUOTE "ARGS-TABLE-LIMIT" QUOTE
                   SPACE "HAS INCORRECT VALUE"
           END-IF
           STOP RUN.

The compiler I used was Micro Focus COBOL 3.2.24.
It works as shown and with the subscripted
NAME-VALUE-PAIR(1).

I see nothing in the LRM, LENGTH intrinsic function
syntax and general rules, to suggest that only one of
these is correct.

Karl,
  Interesting approach.  However, as someone else commented, the '85 Standard 
REPLACE statement had its limitation (only one "active" REPLACE at a time; 
although it could impact many different text words).

As was also indicated, this gets "fixed" in the '02 Standard (and I know you all 
have implemented parts of that).  Have you implemented the REPLACE ALSO 
"enhancements"?  It would seem to me, that the '02 Standard CONSTANT would also 
"solve" this type of application issue.  Therefore, if you (or anyone <G>) had a 
fully '02 compliant compiler, then I think THIS would be a time for CONSTANT 
rather than REPLACE - but that's just a "style" issue.

complete syntactic analysis to find these constant definitions, but for such 
an analysis, the values defined by the constants would already be needed - 
seems to be some cyclic dependency!

I am of the opinion that CONSTANT declaration is preferable to the REPLACE.

Do you implement the "78 level" extension?  I imagine that

78 MYCONST VALUE 25.

and

01  MYCONST CONSTANT 25.

Would work in pretty much the same manner.  

I know that OpenCobol implements the 78-level constant, and it does it in
the "scanner" code.  I believe this means that by the time it gets to the
parser the 78-level constant has already been converted to it's
corresponding literal.  I imagine that the ISO2002 CONSTANT 01 level could
be implemented fairly simply using similar code.

Check out
http://open-cobol.cvs.sourceforge.net/open-cobol/open-cobol/cobc/scanner.l?v
iew=markup if I'm not making any sense...

By the way, can I get you to port you COBOL to the z/VSE operating system. 
:-)
Seriously, I love that you guys are looking to implement so much of the 2002
COBOL standard.  Wish my vendor cared as much.

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Productivity

_(thread depth: 6)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2007-01-01T01:00:29+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4vpn2rF1cr7poU1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4v33ipF1a006cU1@mid.individual.net> <73e30$4592adbc$454920f8$28313@KNOLOGY.NET> <4vgl8dF1bmbn5U1@mid.individual.net> <dnn7p2lh7524u11iuvt77dcchh76c53cfk@4ax.com> <4vis2tF1cbkkdU1@mid.individual.net> <pQDlh.78496$V34.25214@newsfe17.lga>`

```

"P. Raulerson" <paul.rl@raulersons.com> wrote in message 
news:pQDlh.78496$V34.25214@newsfe17.lga...
> Just my two cents - Data Warehousing often requires a really staggering 
> amount of data manipulation and reduction before it is stored in the 
> warehouse. COBOL, in particular BATCH COBOL, is really good for this.

As experience is gained, Data Warehouses become better. Designs improve, 
processing is faster, facilities are more diverse. I know one company where 
NO COBOL has ever been used, and yet their Data Warehouse provides 
incredible support to their business. In particular, cubes can be updated 
from online transactions and automatically consolidated by the warehousing 
software. No batch processing is involved, as far as I know.
>
> Secondly, OLTP systems usually have a batch processing back end to them 
> somewhere or another.

Only because that is how it has "always been done"... :-) (See Michael's 
comment elsewhere).

I addressed this in my response to Frank, in this thread, on 30th December. 
Smarter transactions, running on more powerful processors can obviate batch 
processing. DW software facilitates this.

A properly implemented DW (and I think this may have been Howard's point) 
can obviate a good deal, if not all, of batch processing.


>BATCH processing is just cheaper and faster, and as such will stick around 
>for a long time to come. ;)

I believe it will, but NOT for the reasons you state. It ISN'T cheaper 
(compared to an on-line transaction that sets up accrual in real time) and 
it certainly isn't faster. Adding online accrual to a transaction, for 
example, means it only accesses "today's" data; a batch process would have 
to look at EVERY day's data. You might thik that processing cycles consumed 
should be the same, but it ain't necessarily so...

(Consider an online transaction that calculates interest on an account which 
last had a balance change 3 weeks ago. The transaction can access a 
collection of interest rates for the dates between then and today and 
calculate the accrued interest; it only has to calculate for one period (the 
time since the last balance chage). It "knows" the balance changed because 
it is the transaction that changed it, and it wouldn't be running UNLESS the 
balance changed...

A batch process doing the same job uses a "brute force" approach, looking at 
every account every night, whether the balance changed or not, because it 
can't know whether the balance changed until it looks at it... :-) Total 
processing cycles consumed (especially EXCPs, if you work in an IBM 
environment) will be (much) higher for the batch process.)

This, admittedly contrived, example demonstrates quite clearly the 
fundamental difference between event driven (read, "on-line") and 
non-event-driven (read, "batch") processing. OO lends itself to event driven 
processing; procedural programming doesn't. That is why OO is taking over 
the world... (whether the people using it understand this or not... all they 
know is that Objects are flexible and responsive and designed to handle 
events; procedural code simply isn't...)

Talk to your Ops Manager about the effort required to get everything 
processed through the overnight "Batch window"... You can see Ops people age 
every time a new system with Batch processing is released...The usual 
solution is to throw more hardware at it, but then there is all the 
paperwork and hassle of getting approvals... Politically, it is much easier 
to get approval when online transactions have slowed, because they are so 
much more visible.

I think Batch will be with us for a few years yet, as I stated before, but 
it won't be because it CAN'T be decommissioned; rather, it will be because 
that is what is in place, and it will take a while for the DWs and networks 
to achieve the power that can obviate it, and for managers to wake up to 
that fact.

>COBOL is again, good for that.

Yes, it is. Outstanding, in fact.

And canvas was superb for driving square-rigged sailing vessels.

But you won't find a lot of it on a container ship.

Pete.
```

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2007-01-01T14:23:22+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<4vr64cF1cutp8U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4v33ipF1a006cU1@mid.individual.net> <73e30$4592adbc$454920f8$28313@KNOLOGY.NET> <4vgl8dF1bmbn5U1@mid.individual.net> <dnn7p2lh7524u11iuvt77dcchh76c53cfk@4ax.com> <4vis2tF1cbkkdU1@mid.individual.net> <pQDlh.78496$V34.25214@newsfe17.lga> <4vpn2rF1cr7poU1@mid.individual.net> <1167574958.426550.272040@n51g2000cwc.googlegroups.com> <ce747$4597ebb6$454920f8$18039@KNOLOGY.NET>`

```

"LX-i" <lxi0007@netscape.net> wrote in message 
news:ce747$4597ebb6$454920f8$18039@KNOLOGY.NET...
> Robert Jones wrote:
>> message snipped
…[32 more quoted lines elided]…
>

Sorry, I responded to Robert before I read your post, Daniel.

I agree that payroll is a very good example of a process that is handled 
well by batch  processing, but I also don't think it HAS to be.

I remember many years ago working on a payroll system for Auckland Hospital. 
The design took nearly two years (I didn't do it - I was a programmer). It 
had to cater for every conceivable occupation from janitors to senior 
surgeons, all with their own special awards, penalty rates, holidays, 
payment methods, and payment periods. Just getting information into it (who 
was on leave, who had been  promoted, who needed a final pay because they 
were leaving, how many hours were worked by people who were paid hourly, 
etc. ad nauseum) kept the Payroll department fully employed just entering 
transactions to notify it of exceptions to the underlying base.

If you want a vision here is some holiday induced fantasy... ;-)

Nowadays, I believe all of the base processing could be achieved by stored 
procedures. These procedures could be triggered against each employee 
account on a staggered schedule (say, one every minute, or whatever, 
depending on the number of employees.  - the hospital had around 700, so, if 
you allowed 1 day at the start of the month (say the first banking day of 
the month)  you would do a base calculation for an employee once every two 
minutes. (Hardly a noticeable load on the transaction system.) The result of 
this would be a schedule of payments to go to the Bank on Payday, with a 
line for each employee, keyed on their employee id. During the month, 
transactions for exceptions would occur and each of these would modify the 
line on the schedule for the affected employee, as well as updating their 
account, tax, deductions etc. Come Payday, the schedule is already prepared 
and reflects up to the minute transactions and events. It is sent to the 
Bank, everyone gets their money... Hooray!

Obviously, this is simplistic and assumes that everyone is paid on the same 
day and in the same periodicity, and by direct credit, but it could be 
modified for exceptions to this. For example the schedule could have an 
indicator for the payment method, and trigger a cheque instead of a 
transfer. Separate schedules could be prepared for people who are paid 
weekly, monthly, hourly, whatever. It is feasible and it doesn't require 
daily batch runs or even monthly batch runs with the consequent impact on 
batch windows.

Will it happen? Extremely unlikely, but it could... A small business with a 
small number (say, 50) of employees might find this a very useful way to 
"automate payroll and put it on a back burner".. Because it is on-line it 
would reflect commission payments into the period they were earned (very 
popular with the salesmen), rather than waiting until next month because the 
batch cut-off was missed.

Having said all of the above, I have to agree that payroll is one example of 
something that is best addressed (at least right now), by a batch process.

Pete.
```

"Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message 
news:4vr64cF1cutp8U1@mid.individual.net...
> Having said all of the above, I have to agree that payroll is one example 
> of something that is best addressed (at least right now), by a batch 
> process.

Payroll IS a batch process.

While conventionally the batch size is some multiple of weeks or months, it 
can be a day.. and I guess - in theory anyway - it could be as little as an 
hour; and of course for piecework it could be a piece.

When the underlying business process is itself a batch process, seems to me 
the data processing for same should also be a batch process.

MCM

###### ↳ ↳ ↳ Re: Productivity

_(thread depth: 13)_

- **From:** "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz>
- **Date:** 2007-01-03T10:26:25+13:00
- **Newsgroups:** comp.lang.cobol
- **Message-ID:** `<500103F1dtdh9U1@mid.individual.net>`
- **References:** `<4v33ipF1a006cU1@mid.individual.net> <73e30$4592adbc$454920f8$28313@KNOLOGY.NET> <4vgl8dF1bmbn5U1@mid.individual.net> <dnn7p2lh7524u11iuvt77dcchh76c53cfk@4ax.com> <4vis2tF1cbkkdU1@mid.individual.net> <pQDlh.78496$V34.25214@newsfe17.lga> <4vpn2rF1cr7poU1@mid.individual.net> <1167574958.426550.272040@n51g2000cwc.googlegroups.com> <ce747$4597ebb6$454920f8$18039@KNOLOGY.NET> <4vr64cF1cutp8U1@mid.individual.net> <HS8mh.10367$yC5.3200@newssvr27.news.prodigy.net> <4vt9r2F1dd0ocU1@mid.individual.net> <Dvtmh.28392$hI.3059@newssvr11.news.prodigy.net>`

```

"Michael Mattias" <mmattias@talsystems.com> wrote in message 
news:Dvtmh.28392$hI.3059@newssvr11.news.prodigy.net...
> "Pete Dashwood" <dashwood@removethis.enternet.co.nz> wrote in message 
> news:4vt9r2F1dd0ocU1@mid.individual.net...
…[6 more quoted lines elided]…
> between date-time 'A' and date-time 'B'

An online transaction does that, where values of A and B = 'now'.

As history is simply a collection of 'now' moments, batch processing can be 
obviated by extending the scope of the transaction to do accrual. 
(Previously, we did as little as possible in online transactions to try and 
keep them quick, backing them up with batch processing to pick up what they 
didn't do... My suggestion is, that with techniques like stored database 
procedures that can be triggered to run outside of the actual transaction, 
and running on much mre powerful hardware than was previously available, 
online transaction design CAN now feasibly incorporate more than it did in 
the past.

In essence, the work done by the batch process is 'spread' over the the time 
that multiple transactions run, with the difference that only events which 
cause a change will trigger the accrual. (There is a flaw in this approach 
when it comes to processes like payroll and interest, where the fact that 
time has elapsed (with or without transactions) requires calculation to 
reflect that time has elapsed. However, there are a number of ways in which 
that flaw can be remedied, so batch processing can still be obviated.

If everything is done by transactions that only occur when something needs 
to be changed, the overall processing cycles consumed will be less than the 
case where batch processes are run that look at every object to determine 
whether it changed or not, then process it if it did.

That was my point.

Pete.
```
